<HI>BHAYA1. A demoness, sister of Ka1la who presides over
<>the land of death. She was married to Heti, son of
<>Brahma1 and brother of Praheti. Vidyutkes4a was their
<>son and he married Sa1lakan2t2aka1, daughter of Sandhya1.
<>(Uttara Ra1ma1yan2a).
<HI>BHAYA(M). Him3sa1 is the wife of Adharma. They got
<>a son named Anr2ta and a daughter named Nikr2ti. From
<>them were born Bhaya, Naraka, Ma1ya1 and Vedana1.
<>Of these Ma1ya1 produced Mr2tyu, destroyer of matter.
<>Vedana1 got of her husband Raurava son named Duh2kha.
<>From Mr2tyu were born Vya1dhi, Jara1, S4oka, Tr2s2n2a1
<>and Krodha. (Chapter 20, Agni Pura1n2a). Another
<>version about the birth of Bhaya is found in S4loka 54,
<>Chapter 66 of A1di Parva, M.B. Adharma married Nirr2ti1
<>and to them were born Bhaya, Maha1bhaya and Mr2tyu,
<>three sons of demoniac disposition. These three sons
<>led a sinful life.
<HI>BHAYAN3KARA I. A prince of the country of Sauvi1ra.
<>He was a dependant of Jayadratha. It was this Bhayan3-
<>kara who followed Jayadratha with his flag when he
<>was trying to kidnap Pa1n5ca1li1. Arjuna killed him.
<>(Chapter 265 and 271, Vana Parva, M.B.).
<HI>BHAYAN3KARA II. A sana1tana Vis4vadeva. (Chapter
<>91, Anus4a1sana Parva, M.B.).
<HI>BHAYAN3KARI1. A follower of Subrahman2ya. (S4loka 4,
<>Chapter 46, S4alya Parva, M.B.).
<HI>BHEDI1. A female attendant of Subrahman2ya (M.B.
<>S4alya Parva, Chapter 46, Verse 13).
<HI>BHELA. A disciple of Punarvasu A1treya who was an
<>A1yurveda a1ca1rya. He was a contemporary of Agnives4a
<>and has composed a work on A1yurveda, entitled ‘Bhela-
<>sam3hita1’.
<HI>BHERI1SVATA1. A female attendant of Subrahman2ya.
<>(M.B. S4alya Parva, Chapter 46, Verse 26).
<HI>BHI1MA. Bhi1masena, one of the five Pa1n2d2avas.
<F>1) Since much information about Bhi1ma is given under the captions Dharmaputra, Arjuna, Nakula, Sahadeva and Pa1n5ca1li1 only
<>a brief description of Bhi1ma is attempted under the present heading.</F>
<NI>1) {%Genealogy.%} (See genealogy of Arjuna).
<NI>2) {%Birth and childhood.%} King Vicitravi1rya of Candra
<>vam3s4a (lunar dynasty) had two sons called Dhr2ta-
<>ra1s2t2ra and Pa1n2d2u. The Kauravas (Duryodhana etc.) were
<>sons born to Dhr2tara1s2t2ra of his wife Ga1ndha1ri1, and the [Page129-a+ 65]
<>Pa1n2d2avas were the sons of Pa1n2d2u and his wives Kunti1
<>and Ma1dri1. Dharmaputra, Bhi1ma and Arjuna were
<>the sons of Kunti1, and Nakula and Sahadeva of
<>Ma1dri1.
<F>1) The Pa1n2d2avas were not in fact direct issues of Pa1n2d2u. For details see Kunti1.</F>
<NI>Kunti1 directed a mantra gifted to her by Durva1sas to-
<>wards Va1yubhagava1n (the wind-god) and the result
<>was the birth of Bhi1ma. Hence he is called Va1yu-putra
<>(son of the wind-god). At the time of his birth a celestial
<>voice announced that the boy would grow up to be the
<>strongest among the strong. (A1di Parva, Chapter 122,
<>Verse 14). On the tenth day after birth the child Bhi1ma
<>fell from his mother's lap on a rock. Bhi1ma was not
<>injured in any manner by that fall, although it crushed
<>the rock into power. (This story is told in the southern
<>texts of the Maha1bha1rata in Chapter 132 of A1di Parva).
<>The naming ceremony of the child was performed by
<>the Mahars2is, who stayed at S4atas4r2n3ga. Kas4yapa Maha-
<>rs2i, family priest of Vasudeva performed the ceremonies
<>like wearing of the sacred thread. Bhi1ma learned fight-
<>ing with the gada1 (club or mace) from S4uka, the famous
<>Ra1jars2i.
<NI>The Kauravas and the Pa1n2d2avas spent their childhood
<>in Hastina1pura. Dron2a1ca1rya taught them fighting
<>with weapons. The Kauravas and the Pa1n2d2avas often
<>engaged themselves in children's games. In all such
<>games Bhi1ma used to hurt and defeat the Kauravas,
<>and to this fact the unending hatred of the Kauravas
<>towards Bhi1ma owed its origin. Once they adminis-
<>tered poison to Bhi1ma who fell down unconscious, and
<>then they threw him into the depths of the Gan3ga1
<>(Ganges). Going deeper and deeper in the waters
<>Bhi1ma, at last, reached the Na1galoka, where the na1gas
<>(serpents) bit him which neutralized the effects of the
<>poison in his body. There he got acquainted with a
<>na1ga called A1ryaka, who introduced him to Va1suki,
<>king of the na1gas, and Va1suki presented him with much
<>wealth and other costly gems. But, what use was all
<>this wealth to Bhi1ma? Then Va1suki agreed to give him
<>a divine drink, which would give the user of it the
<>strength of thousand elephants. Bhi1ma drank at one
<>draught eight pot-fulls of that divine drink, and thus
<>became tremendously strong. But, he had to wait in
<>Na1galoka for eight days so that the drink might be
<>thoroughly assimilated, and on the ninth day the na1gas
<>saw him off in all pomp and splendour. Bhi1ma returned
<>to his mother and brothers and consoled them, who
<>were terribly anxious at his absence.
<NI>When the training of the princes in the use of weapons
<>was over a competition or test was conducted. Duryo-
<>dhana and Bhi1ma entered into a ‘club-fight’, and when
<>Karn2a tried to intervene in the fight his nobility was
<>questioned by Bhi1ma. Duryodhana then insulted Bhi1ma.
<>Arjuna agreed to present King Drupada before Dron2a1-
<>ca1rya as gurudaks2ina1 to him. In the fierce war the
<>Pa1n2d2avas fought with Drupada, Bhi1ma annihilated the
<>elephant division of the latter's army. And, afterwards
<>Bhi1ma underwent higher training in club-war at the
<>hands of Balabhadrara1ma. (A1di Parva, Chapter 136,
<>Verse 4).
<NI>3) {%The Pa1n2d2avas left Hastina1pura.%} As enmity between
<>the Kauravas and the Pa1n2d2avas began growing stronger
<>and stronger, Duryodhana, with his father's permission,
<>removed the Pa1n2d2avas to va1ran2a1vata and settled them
<>there. They were put up there in a palace specially [Page129-b+ 64]
<>made of lac. The Pa1n2d2avas divined the secret of it and
<>escaped from the fire, when the palace was set fire to.
<>Verse 10, Chapter 147 of the A1di Parva states that it
<>was Bhi1ma, who set fire to the palace. Escaping thus
<>through a tunnel the Pa1n2d2avas travelled a great distance
<>in the forest. Kunti1 and four of her sons got tired by the
<>exertions of the travel and were forced to sit down for
<>rest on the way. Bhi1ma, continued the journey carrying
<>the mother and his four brothers on his shoulders. With
<>their entry into Hid2im3ba forest the weakness left them,
<>and they became their former selves.
<NI>4) {%Hid2im3ba killed.%} Kunti1 devi1 and four sons slept under
<>the shade of a tree at dusk, and Bhi1ma kept guard over
<>them. There dwelt in the forest a Ra1ks2asa called Hid2im3ba
<>with his sister, Hid2im3bi1. Hid2im3ba looked around that
<>particular day from the top of a tree, and detecting
<>Bhi1ma his mouth watered. He deputed Hid2imbi1 to
<>bring Bhi1ma over to him. Hid2im3bi1 approached Bhi1ma,
<>whose fine figure kindled feelings of love in her. She
<>desired to have him as husband. Hid2im3bi1 having not
<>returned even after a long time Hidim3ba went over to
<>the spot, and there finding Hid2im3bi1 in love-talks with
<>Bhi1ma he got terribly angry. He wanted to kill Hid2im3bi1.
<>Bhi1ma, who could not suffer the killing of a woman in
<>his presence rushed against Hid2im3ba, The noise of the
<>fight awakened the other Pa1n2d2avas from sleep, and at
<>the instance of Arjuna, Bhi1ma killed Hid2im3ba. Thus
<>rendered helpless and forlorn Hid2im3bi1 again craved
<>Bhi1ma for love. On the suggestion of Kunti1, whose
<>heart melted at the sight of Hid2im3bi1's helplessness Bhi1ma
<>took her as his wife. But, one condition was stipulated
<>for their enjoying the honey-moon. The condition was
<>that they might enjoy honey-moon, from dawn to dusk
<>in the sky and on mountain tops, Hid2im3bi1, who was
<>endowed with magic powers carrying Bhi1ma with her.
<>And, after dusk Bhi1ma was to be returned to Kunti1.
<>Accordingly Bhi1ma and Hid2im3bi1 spent one year, and
<>to them was born a son called Ghat2otkaca. Promising
<>that he shall return when wanted, Ghat2otkaca with his
<>mother went into the forest. The Pa1n2d2avas also left
<>for the village called Ekacakra1. (A1di Parva, Chapters
<>147-154).
<NI>5) {%Killing of Baka and the wedding of Pa1n5ca1li1.%} While at
<>Ekacakra1 Bhi1ma killed the Ra1ks2asa called Baka and
<>freed the people of the village from their distress.
<>Afterwards the Pa1n2d2avas attended the Svayamvara
<>(free choice of the husband by woman) of Pa1n5ca1li1,
<>who became their wife. There Bhi1ma defeated S4alya
<>in fight. And, the Pa1n2d2avas duly returned to Hastina1-
<>pura. (For details see Baka, Pa1n5ca1li1 and Arjuna).
<NI>6) {%Again to forest.%} On their return to Hastinapura the
<>Pa1n2d2avas took their residence in the palace built by
<>Maya. There Maya presented a magnificent club to
<>Bhi1ma. (Sabha1 Parva, Chapter 3, Verse 18). It was
<>S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a, lord of Dva1raka1 who served as the right hand
<>of the Pa1n2d2avas. Jara1sandha, who was then King of
<>Magadha fought with Kr2s2n2a eighteen times and got
<>defeated. Yet he did not yield, and at last Kr2s2n2a decided
<>to do away with him. Kr2s2n2a, Arjuna and Bhi1ma, in
<>disguise, set out for Magadha. They entered Jara1sandha's
<>palace and challenged him to a duel. Bhi1ma and Jara1-
<>sandha clashed, and at the instance of Kr2s2n2a Bhi1ma
<>rent the latter in two and threw him on the ground.
<>Though Jara1sandha was alive again, Bhi1ma rent him [Page130-a+ 61]
<>in two and threw away the two parts to two places.
<>(M.B. Sabha1 Parva, Southern Text, Chapter 24).
<NI>The main impediments and thorns in their way thus
<>having been removed, Dharmaputra decided to perform
<>Ra1jasu1ya. Bhi1ma was deputed to conquer all the king-
<>doms in the eastern part of India. Bhi1ma achieved the
<>object and returned with great wealth to Indraprastha.
<>Though Bhi1ma got ready to kill S4is4upa1la, who alone
<>refused to acknowledge the suzerainty of Yudhis2t2hira,
<>he also yielded on the tactful advice of Bhi1s2ma. The
<>Ra1jasu1ya Yajn5a went off quite successfully. It was
<>Bhi1ma, who, after the Yajn5a was over, took Bhi1s2ma and
<>Yudhis2t2hira to Hastina1pura. Afterwards, in the contest
<>in the game of dice played between Dharmaputra and
<>Duryodhana, the Pa1n2d2avas lost everything. The Kaura-
<>vas brought Pa1n5ca1li1 into the assembly hall and attempted
<>to strip her naked in public. Bhi1ma who got enraged at
<>this shouted that the hands of Yudhis2t2hira who played
<>dice should be burnt in fire. (A1di Parva, Chapter 68,
<>Verse 6). And, Bhi1ma took then and there the terrible
<>pledge that he would, with his hands stained by blood
<>from the chest of Dus4s4a1sana, who tried to rip Pa1n5ca1li1
<>naked, tie up Pa1n5ca1li1's hair which got untied in the
<>scuffle. He also swore that he would break the thigh of
<>Duryodhana. In uncontrollable rage Bhi1ma also shouted
<>that he would turn into ashes all those who took part in
<>the game of dice. Bhi1ma took also the vow that all the
<>Kauravas would be killed.
<NI>According to the terms and conditions laid down with
<>regard to the contest in the game of dice the Pa1n2d2avas
<>went into the Ka1myaka forest to live there for twelve
<>years and then to live incognito for one year.
<NI>7) {%Life in forest and life incognito.%} There lived in Ka1m-
<>yaka forest a Ra1ks2asa called Kirmi1ra, brother of Bala,
<>whom Bhi1ma had killed on an earlier occasion. Kirmi1ra,
<>who was awaiting an opportunity to avenge the murder
<>of his brother, now clashed with Bhi1ma in the forest.
<>Bhi1ma did very easily kill him. (For details see Kir-
<>mi1ra).
<NI>Thus the Pa1n2d2avas spent their days once again in the
<>Ka1myaka forest under the spiritual leadership of sage
<>Dhaumya. They thought about their lost kingdom.
<>Should they go to war against the Kauravas or should
<>they spend the rest of their lives in the exercise of dha1rmic
<>injunctions? At one time Bhi1ma advised Yudhis2t2hira
<>against war; but on another occasion he pleaded vehe-
<>mently in favour of war. It was during this time that
<>Arjuna went to the Hima1layas to please S4iva by penance
<>and get from him the Pa1s4upata1stra. (Arrow called
<>Pa1s4upata). The Pa1n2d2avas naturally got nervous and
<>upset at the rather long absence of Arjuna; Bhi1ma was
<>more anxious and sorry than the others. Then the
<>Pa1n2d2avas set out in search of Arjuna, and travelled upto
<>Mount Gandhama1dana. Then the party got so tired
<>that they could not proceed any further. Pa1n5ca1li1 fell
<>down fainting. Then Bhi1ma remembered Ghat2otkaca,
<>who appeared before his father (Bhi1ma) at once. As
<>directed by Bhi1ma Ghat2otkaca mounted the Pa1n2davas
<>on his shoulders and the journey continued. They
<>reached the A1s4rama of Narana1ra1yan2as, and rested there
<>for six days. One day the wind blowing from the north- [Page130-b+ 65]
<>east dropped near Pa1n5ca1li1 a Saugandhika flower. And,
<>Bhi1ma set out in the north-east direction to fetch saugan-
<>dhika flowers for Pa1n5ca1li1, who felt a special liking for
<>them.
<NI>Walking and walking Bhi1ma entered Kadali1vana.
<>Hanu1ma1n, his skin wrinkled and hair grey due to old
<>age, was living in this forest. He obstructed the path of
<>Bhi1ma. Hanu1ma1n awoke from sleep and raised his tail
<>with a terrific sound. Bhi1ma walked upto the place
<>whence the sound was heard.
<F>1. When raised, Hanu1ma1n's tail was as high in the sky as the flag of Indra, and produced a thunderous sound. As though the
<>mountains were vomitting through their mouth, the sound produced by the raising of the tail shook the mountains. Drowning the trumpeting of
<>excited elephants the sound reverberated all around the mountains. Hearing the sound Bhi1ma, his whole body horripilated entered the
<>forest in the direction of the sound. In the middle of Kadali1vana, on a mighty rock, Bhi1ma saw Hanu1ma1n.</F> (Vanaparva, Chapter
<>146). In the clash that ensued between Hanu1ma1n and
<>Bhi1ma the former came out victorious. Hanu1ma1n,
<>however, congratulated Bhi1ma and directed him on the
<>path to the saugandhika forest.
<NI>Bhi1masena reached the saugandhika forest, which was
<>being guarded by the Ra1ks2asas called Krodhavas4as.
<>Bhi1ma overcame them, collected the flowers and return-
<>ing with them stayed in the Badarika1s4rama with his
<>brothers and Pa1n5ca1li1. Here it was that Bhi1ma killed
<>Jat2a1sura. (For details see Jat2a1sura II).
<NI>Four years were thus spent; yet Arjuna had not returned.
<>The Pa1n2d2avas continued their journey northward.
<>On the 17th day they came to the A1s4rama of Vr2s2aparva1
<>in the Hima1layas. They were duly received by the
<>mahars2i, who directed them in their onward journey.
<>Continuing the journey they reached the A1s4rama of
<>A1rs2t2is2en2a whence, after crossing various mountain peaks
<>and still walking they reached Kubera's Alaka1puri1 when
<>a Yaks2a called Man2ima1n obstructed their further pro-
<>gress. Bhi1ma killed Man2ima1n and the other Yaks2as who
<>rushed to his support. Finally Kubera himself saw
<>Bhi1ma and blessed the Pa1n2d2avas.
<NI>While they were returning from Kubera's palace Bhi1ma
<>was caught by a python. But, it was really Nahus2a
<>transformed into a python on account of a curse. Bhi1ma
<>killed it and it assumed its original form as Nahus2a.
<>(See Agastya, Para 8). By this time Arjuna had obtained
<>Pa1s4upata1stra from S4iva and he duly returned to his
<>brothers, and the Pa1n2d2avas continued their journey in
<>the forest.
<NI>Meantime, knowing that the Pa1n2d2avas were put up in
<>Dvaitavana, the Kauravas started for their dwelling
<>place in a procession led by Duryodhana with the army
<>and camped nearly two furlongs away from a pool in
<>Dvaitavana. While thus camping Duryodhana clashed
<>with a Gandharva called Citrasena, who with a number
<>of his comrades came to the pool for water games,
<>and in the encounter the latter made Duryodhana
<>prisoner. Bhi1masena who witnessed the scene very much
<>laughed at Duryodhana. But, Arjuna intervened and
<>set free Duryodhana and others.
<NI>The Pa1n2d2avas again entered the Ka1myaka forest, and
<>it was at that time that Jayadratha abducted Pa1n5ca1li1.
<>Bhi1ma killed Kot2ika1sya who acted on behalf of Jaya-
<>dratha. (See Kot2ika1sya). Moreover Bhi1ma captured
<>Jayadratha, got his head shaved clean and declared that
<>he was a slave of Dharmaputra. It was here at Dvaita-
<>vana that Dharmadeva tested the Pa1n2d2avas, who had
<>gone to a nearby pool to fetch water; all the Pa1n2d2avas
<>except Yudhis2t2hira died at the pool, but were brought
<>back to life again. (See Dharmaputra, Para 7). The [Page131-a+ 64]
<>twelve years’ forest-life of the Pa1n2d2avas now came to
<>an end.
<NI>According to the advice of Dharmadeva the Pa1n2d2avas
<>selected the Vira1t2a palace for their life incognito, Bhi1ma-
<>sena assuming the name Vallava (Valala). And, here
<>Bhi1ma killed in a duel Ji1mu1ta, the pugilist. (See Ji1mu1ta
<>II). It was also here that Bhi1ma killed Ki1caka and the
<>Upaki1cakas. (See Ki1caka). On another occasion, at
<>the instance of Yudhis2t2hira Bhi1ma took Sudharma1, King
<>of Das4a1rn2a to Yudhis2t2hira captive; but he was later set
<>free. Next year the Pa1n2d2avas defeated Duryodhana in
<>the fight in connection with the theft of the cows of the
<>Vira1t2a King, and then they declared that their forest
<>life and life incognito were over.
<NI>8) {%Bhi1ma in the great war.%} Even after the return of the
<>Pa1n2d2avas after the forest life and life incognito the
<>Kauravas refused to give them half of the kingdom. So,
<>both the parties began preparations for war. Given here-
<>under is the main incident relating to Bhi1ma from this
<>period to the Svarga1rohan2a (going to Heaven) of the
<>Pa1n2d2avas after relinquishing the kingdom in favour of
<>Pari1ks2it, including their victory in war and the adminis-
<>tration of the country.
<NI>(1) San5jaya described to Dhr2tara1s2t2ra the prowess and
<>achievements of Bhi1ma. (Udyoga Parva, Chapter 50).
<NI>(2) S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a before leaving for the Kaurava assembly
<>for compromise talks asked for the views of Bhi1ma about
<>the whole problem, and Bhi1ma opined that peace was
<>preferable to war. (Udyoga Parva, Chapter 74).
<NI>(3) When S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a admonished Bhi1ma he opted for war
<>and waxed eloquent about his heroism and prowess.
<>(Udyoga Parva, Chapter 76).
<NI>(4) Bhi1ma wanted S4ikhan2d2i1 to be appointed chief of the
<>army. (Udyoga Parva, Chapter 161).
<NI>(5) Bhi1ma sent back with an insulting reply Ulu1ka,
<>who was sent by Duryodhana to the Pa1n2d2avas with a
<>message. (Udyoga Parva, Chapter 163).
<NI>(6) Bhi1ma questioned Dharmaputra who, when the
<>armies had taken position on opposite sides, went on foot
<>to the Kaurava assembly without bow and arrows.
<>(Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter 48, Verse 17).
<NI>(7) The world shuddered at the war cry of Bhi1ma.
<>(Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter 44, Verse 8).
<NI>(8) On the first day of the war Bhi1ma fought a duel with
<>Duryodhana. (Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter 45, Verse 19).
<NI>(9) In the fight with the Kalin3gas Bhi1ma killed S4akra-
<>deva. (Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter 54, Verse 24).
<NI>(10) Bhi1ma killed Bha1numa1n. (Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter
<>54, Verse 39).
<NI>(11) He killed Satyadeva and S4alya, who guarded the
<>chariot wheels of S4ruta1yus, King of Kalin3ga. (Bhi1s2ma
<>Parva, Chapter 54, Verse 76).
<NI>(12) Killed Ketuma1n. (Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter 54,
<>Verse 77).
<NI>(13) Annihilated the elephant division of the Kaurava
<>army, and rivers of blood flowed. (Bhi1s2ma Parva,
<>Chapter 54, Verse 103).
<NI>(14) Defeated Duryodhana. (Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter 58,
<>Verse 16).
<NI>(15) Fought against Bhi1s2ma. (Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter
<>63, Verse 1).
<NI>(16) Fought against the whole lot of Kauravas, and in
<>this fight eight sons of Dhr2tara1s2t2ra viz. Sena1pati, Jara1-
<>sandha, Sus2en2a, Ugra, Vi1raba1hu, Bhi1ma, Bhi1maratha [Page131-b+ 64]
<>and Sulocana were killed. (Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter 64,
<>Verse 32).
<NI>(17) Fought a fierce war against Bhi1s2ma. (Bhi1s2ma Parva,
<>Chapter 72, Verse 21).
<NI>(18) Fought with Duryodhana. (Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chap-
<>ter 72, Verse 17).
<NI>(19) Defeated Duryodhana the second time. (Bhi1s2ma
<>Parva, Chapter 79, Verse 11).
<NI>(20) Defeated Kr2tavarma1. (Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter 82,
<>Verse 60).
<NI>(21) Killed Bhi1s2ma's charioteer. (Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chap-
<>ter 88, Verse 12).
<NI>(22) Killed eight more sons of Dhr2tara1s2t2ra. (Chapter 88,

<NI>(23) Struck by the arrow of Bhi1ma, Dron2a1ca1rya fell down

<NI>(24) Killed nine more sons of Dhr2tara1s2t2ra. (Bhi1s2ma

<NI>(25) Defeated Ba1lhi1ka. (Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter 104,

<NI>(26) Fought a duel with Bhu1ris4ravas. (Bhi1s2ma Parva,

<NI>(27) Killed ten maha1rathi1s (heroes in chariot war) of
<>the Kaurava army. (Bhi1s2ma Parva, Chapter 113).
<NI>(28) Dhr2tara1s2t2ra applauded the prowess of Bhi1ma.

<NI>(29) Bhi1ma fought with Vivim3s4ati. (Dron2a Parva, Chap-

<NI>(30) Defeated S4alya in club fight. (Dron2a Parva, Chapter

<NI>(31) Fought with Durmars2an2a. (Dron2a Parva, Chapter

<NI>(32) Killed An3ga, king of the Mleccha tribe. (Dron2a

<NI>(33) Fought with the elephant of Bhagadatta, was

<NI>(34) Attacked Karn2a and killed fifteen warriors of his.

<NI>(36) Fought with Alambus2a and came out victorious.

<NI>8) {%Bhi1ma's conceit put down.%} While, after the great war,
<>the Pa1n2d2avas and S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a were discussing several
<>matters all the Pa1n2d2avas except Bhi1ma said they owed
<>their success in war to Kr2s2n2a. But, Bhi1ma, in all haughti-
<>ness claimed the credit for victory to his personal prowess.
<>With the object of putting down this conceit on the part
<>of Bhi1ma, S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a, with Bhi1ma seated along with him
<>on Garud2a, set out on a journey to the south. After
<>crossing the sea and Mount Subela S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a, pointing
<>out to Bhi1ma a lake twelve yojanas wide and lying
<>near Lan3ka1, asked him to find out the source of the lake
<>and return with the information. Though Bhi1ma walked
<>some distance he could not find out its source. Not only
<>that, all the warriors there jointly attacked Bhi1ma, and
<>finding himself impotent to counter the attack he ran
<>back to S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a for refuge. Then S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a with his
<>ring clipped and threw away the lake, and said to Bhi1ma
<>as follows:--“This is the skull of Kumbhakarn2a killed
<>by S4ri1 Ra1ma in the Ra1ma-Ra1van2a war. The warriors
<>who attacked you are the asuras called ‘Sarogeyas’.”
<>These words of the lord put down Bhi1ma's conceit,
<>and he apologised to Kr2s2n2a. (Skanda Pura1n2a, 1.2.66).
<NI>9) {%Death.%} After entrusting matters of administration of
<>the country to Pari1ks2it the Pa1n2d2avas set out on their
<>great journey. Yudhis2t2hira walking in the front, they
<>started for Kaila1sa. During the course of their journey
<>Pa1n5ca1li1, Sahadeva, Nakula and Arjuna one after the
<>other fell down dead. Bhi1ma asked Yudhis2t2hira the
<>reason for the deaths and he was given suitable answers
<>by the latter. At last when Bhi1ma too was about to fall
<>down and die he asked the reason thereof, and Yudhis2-
<>t2hira replied that Bhi1ma's over-eating was the reason.
<>Afterwards when Dharmaputra entered Heaven he
<>found his brothers had already their seats there. (See
<>Arjuna, Para 31).

<HI>BHI1MA VI. A S4u1dra who attained Svarga as on his head
<>fell water with which the feet of a brahmin were washed.
<>The following story about him occurs on page 619 of
<>the Padmapura1n2a.
<NI>In the dva1para yuga there lived a S4u1dra called Bhi1ma,
<>who engaged himself in the profession of Vais4yas. An
<>outcaste from practices pertaining to S4u1dras he enjoyed
<>life with a Vais4ya woman. He was a terrible fellow, who
<>had killed many brahmins, and also enjoyed the wives
<>of many elderly people including his teachers. He was
<>a robber as well. Once he went to a brahmin house,
<>and with the object of robbing his wealth spoke to him
<>in a pathetic tone as follows:--“Respected sire, you
<>will please listen to my grievance. You appear to be kind-
<>hearted. Please give me some rice, or else I will die this
<>very moment.”
<NI>Brahmin:--“Oh hungry guest! There is no one here
<>to cook food. I shall give you daily some rice, which
<>you may cook yourself. I have neither father, mother,
<>son, brothers, wife nor any other relatives. All of them
<>are dead and gone. The unfortunate fellow that I am,
<>I am staying here alone. No servants or others here.”
<>Bhi1ma:--“Oh revered brahmin! I too am a lonely
<>person. I shall live here for ever serving you. I am a
<>S4u1dra.”
<NI>These words of Bhi1ma pleased the brahmin so much that
<>he cooked some food quickly and served the S4u1dra with
<>it. He stayed with the brahmin from that day onwards.
<>His idea was to rob the brahmin of his wealth at some
<>convenient time and get away. But, since he used to
<>pour on his head everyday the water with which the
<>brahmin's feet were washed he got redemption from all
<>his sins.
<NI>One night a thief got into the brahmin's room to steal his
<>earnings. Seeing the thief Bhi1ma rushed at him to give
<>him a good thrashing. But, the thief, in the twinkling
<>of an eye, cut off Bhi1ma's head and escaped from the
<>scene. At once there came down the attendants of Lord
<>Vis2n2u to lead Bhi1ma to Vaikun2t2ha. A divine chariot
<>drawn by Ra1jaham3sas (swans) also came down. Bhi1ma
<>got into the chariot and reached the abode of Vis2n2u.

<HI>BHI1S2MA.
<NI>1) {%Genealogy.%} From Vis2n2u were descended in the follow-
<>ing order--Brahma1-Atri-Candra-Budha-Puru1ravas-
<>A1yus-Nahus2a-Yaya1ti-Pu1ru-Janamejaya-Pra1cinva1-
<>Pravi1ra-Namasyu-Vi1tabhaya-S4un2d2u-Bahuvidha-
<>Sam3ya1ti-Rahova1di-Raudra1s4va-Matina1ra-Santu-
<>rodha-Dus2yanta-Bharata-Suhotra-Suhota1-Gala-Gardda
<>Suketu-Br2hatks2etra-Hasti-Ajami1d2ha-R2ks2a-Samva-
<>ran2a-Kuru-Jahnu-Suratha-Vid2u1ratha-Sa1rvabhauma-
<>Jayatsena-Ravyaya-Bha1vuka-Cakroddhata-Deva1tithi-
<>R2ks2a-Bhi1ma-Prati1pa-S4antanu-Bhi1s2ma.
<NI>2) {%Birth and Boyhood.%} Bhi1s2ma's name in his boyhood was
<>Devavrata. He was the eighth son of S4antanu, a king
<>of the lunar dynasty and Gan3ga1devi1. This boy was the
<>human embodiment of Dyau, one of the As2t2avasus.
<>S4antanu, his father was the re-birth of another king,
<>Maha1bhis2eka. The story concerning this, as given in
<>the Maha1bha1rata is as follows:--
<NI>King Maha1bhis2eka after his death, attained Vis2n2uloka.
<>Once he went to visit Brahma1 at Satyaloka. At that
<>time Gan3ga1devi1 was also present in Brahma1's assembly.
<>In that pious atmosphere, a gentle breeze began to blow
<>and Gan3ga1devi1's clothes were slightly deranged. Just
<>at that moment, Maha1bhis2eka took a stealthy glance at
<>her and she also returned that glance. This was noted
<>by Brahma1 who turned both of them into human beings
<>by a curse. Gan3ga1devi begged pardon and Brahma1
<>lifted the curse and blessed her that the As2t2avasus would
<>come to the earth to be born as her sons and that after-
<>wards she could come back to Heaven. After that
<>Gan3ga1devi1 was born as a mortal woman in the world
<>under the name Gan3ga1 and she spent her days in the
<>forests near the Gan3ga1 river valleys.
<NI>In those days the ruler of the Lunar dynasty was a king
<>named Prati1pa. Having no children, he went to the
<>bank of the river Gan3ga1 and performed tapas there.
<>Gan3ga1devi1 who was moving about in the forests near-
<>by, saw the King deeply absorbed in his tapas. She
<>approached him and sat on his right thigh. She wanted
<>the King to be her husband. He explained to her that
<>the right thigh is the proper seat of a daughter-in-law [Page135-a+ 65]
<>and so she would become his son's wife in due course.
<>In course of time, Prati1pa had a son, S4antanu, born
<>to him. When S4antanu grew up into a young man, one
<>day he went for a hunt to the Gan3ga1-valley and there he
<>met Gan3ga1devi1. He fell in love with her at first sight
<>and courted her. Gan3ga1devi1 agreed to become his wife
<>on condition that he should not say anything to displease
<>her and if he violated that condition she would leave him.
<>The king accepted the condition and they became man
<>and wife.
<NI>At about that time, the wife of Dyo, one of the As2t2a-
<>vasus, happened to see the sacrificial cow of the sage
<>Vasis2t2ha and wished to have it. She expressed her
<>desire to her husband, Dyo. Dyo, with the other seven
<>vasus went and took away by force, Vasis2t2ha's cow.
<>Vasis2t2ha in his anger cursed the As2t2avasus to be born as
<>mortals. They repented and begged pardon from
<>Vasis2t2ha. The sage told them that all of them would
<>be born as the sons of Gan3ga1devi1 and all except Dyo,
<>who actually stole the cow, would return to Heaven
<>at the time of birth itself. As for Dyo, he would continue
<>to live in the world for a long time, as an adventurous
<>hero.
<NI>Gan3ga1devi1 became pregnant and gave birth to her first
<>child. She carried the child to the river Gan3ga1 and
<>threw it into the river. S4antanu who followed her up
<>to the river bank, did not say anything against her,
<>remembering his promise.
<NI>Seven children were born to her and she threw all of them
<>into the river in this way. When she gave birth to the
<>eighth child, S4antanu insisted that he would not allow
<>her to throw away that child into the river. As he had
<>violated the condition, the angry Gan3ga1devi1 left the
<>palace with her child. She named it Devavrata and
<>brought him up in the forest. The sage Vasis2t2ha and
<>Gan3ga1devi1 taught him all branches of knowledge.
<>Thirtytwo years later, the king went to the same forest
<>for hunting. He saw a handsome boy stopping the
<>flow of the river Gan3ga1. Getting interested in the boy,
<>the King approached him. But by that time he had
<>disappeared. The King prayed to Gan3ga1devi1 to give
<>back the child. She appeared with the child and after
<>handing over the child to him vanished. The king
<>returned to the palace with the child. (M.B. A1di
<>Parva, Chapters 95-100).
<NI>3) {%The name Bhi1s2ma.%} Devavrata was anointed, as
<>heir-apparent. One day King S4antanu reached the
<>forest near the Gan3ga1 river valley, for hunting. As he
<>was hunting, absorbed in the beauty of the forest scenery,
<>he felt the perfume of musk filling the air in the forest.
<>He wondered from where it could come. He went on
<>and on trying to find out the source of this smell until
<>he reached the cottage of a fisherman. The fisherman
<>had a daughter named Satyavati1. It was from her that
<>the fragrance of musk spread all around.
<F>1) Satyavati1's original name was Ka1li1. The fisherman got her from the stomach of a fish. (See the word Adrika1). Since she
<>had the smell of fish she got the name of “Matsyagandhi1.” She used to assist a fisherman in his work as a ferryman in the river Gan3ga1.
<>Once the sage Para1s4ara happened to get into her boat and he fell deeply in love with her. The sage removed the smell of fish from her and gave
<>her the perfume of musk instead. By this mystic power he created a mist at noon and under its cover, he had a sexual union with her. As
<>a result of it the child Kr2s2n2a (Vya1sa) was born. The child immediately left the mother to perform tapas in the forest after promising to
<>return to her whenever she wished for his presence. Although she gave birth to a child, Para1s4ara blessed that she would again remain a
<>virgin. The whole episode remained a secret. As usual, Satyavati1 returned to the fisherman's cottage in the evening and continued to
<>live with him. It is at this stage that S4antanu was attracted by the perfume of musk and came to the cottage where he met Satyavati1.</F> The king
<>fell in love with her at first sight. He asked the fisherman
<>to give the girl in marriage to him. But the brave fisher- [Page135-b+ 57]
<>man did not yield to the king's demand immediately.
<>He laid down several conditions, one of which was that
<>Satyavati1's sons should succeed to the throne of S4antanu.
<>The king was in a fix. Devavrata was the eldest son and
<>heir-apparent. To deny kingship to his sons would be
<>highly improper. Unable to find a solution to this diffi-
<>cult problem, the king returned to the palace, much
<>depressed and gloomy. There he avoided all company
<>and took to his bed, passing his time in sadness and
<>solitude.
<NI>When Devavrata knew about his father's condition, he
<>called the Ministers and asked them about it. They
<>told him everything in details. At once, without inform-
<>ing even his father, Devavrata went to the fisherman's
<>cottage on the bank of the river Gan3ga1 and begged for
<>Satyavati1 on behalf of his father. The fisherman repeated
<>his former condition. Devavrata agreed that Satya-
<>vati1's son shall be given the right of Kingship. The
<>fisherman pointed out that disputes were likely to arise
<>between Devavrata's sons and Satyavati1's children regar-
<>ding the right of succession to the throne. At once
<>Devavrata stood up and made a solemn pledge that he
<>would remain a bachelor for life. The fisherman gave
<>Satyavati1 to Devavrata to be taken to the King. Deva-
<>vrata took her to the palace and presented her to his
<>father. The King, when he came to know of the part
<>played by his son in the matter, rose from his bed and
<>embraced Devavrata with tears of joy and gratitude.
<>The gods showered flowers on the scene. Because he had
<>taken such a solemn oath, it was declared that hence-
<>forth he would be known by the name “BHI1S2MA”.
<>The loving father S4antanu also gave him a boon that
<>Bhi1s2ma would die only when he wished. (M.B., A1di
<>Parva, Chapter 100).

<HI>BHR2GU.

<NI>2) {%Birth.%}
<Poem>“Utsam3ga1d Na1rado jajn5e

<NI>From these lines we see that Bhr2gu was born from
<>Brahma1's skin (tvak). But in M.B. A1di Parva, 5th
<>Chapter, we find another version regarding his birth.
<>In that passage we read that Bhr2gu was born from
<>“Vahni” (fire). In the light of these two statements, we
<>may examine Bhr2gu's birth.
<NI>Bhr2gu had two incarnations. The first time he was born
<>from Brahma1's skin. In course of time, the sage Bhr2gu
<>became famous. In the Daks2aya1ga, this sage was pre-
<>sent as one of the R2tviks (officiating priests). On that
<>occasion, Sati1devi1 who was in rage and grief because
<>her husband (S4iva) was not invited to the ya1ga, commit-
<>ted suicide by jumping into the sacrificial fire. Hearing
<>about this, S4iva was enraged and the monster spirits who
<>emerged from his matted locks caught hold of the
<>R2tviks. Bha1gavata caturtha skandha says that the Bhu1ta
<>named Nandi1s4vara, who emerged from S4iva's locks,
<>caught hold of Bhr2gu and killed him.
<NI>Therefore the Bhr2gu who was born from Brahma1's
<>skin must be considered as having died at Daks2aya1ga.
<>Bhr2gu was born again in Vaivasvata Manvantara.
<>This second birth was at the famous Brahmayajn5a
<>of Varun2a. He was reborn from fire, as Brahma1's son.
<>This child who was born from Brahma1's semen which
<>fell in the sacrificial fire, was brought up by Varun2a
<>and his wife Cars2an2i1. Consequently Bhr2gu is referred
<>to as “Varun2aputra” and “Cars2an2i1putra” in some
<>Pura1n2as. Since he was born at Varun2a's ya1ga he is
<>sometimes called “Va1run2i1 Bhr2gu”.

<NI>4) {%Bhr2gu cursed Maha1vis2n2u.%} Once a terrible war broke
<>out between Devas and Asuras. In that war, not only
<>were the Asuras defeated but many of them were also
<>killed. Diti, the mother of the Asuras, with tears in her
<>eyes, complained to Bhr2gupati. Puloma1, Mother of
<>S4ukra, promised to find a remedy for this somehow.
<>She at once went to the forest and started a tapas for
<>the annihilation of the Devas. As the tapas gained
<>force, the Devas were alarmed and they sought the
<>protection of Maha1vis2n2u. Maha1vis2n2u used his
<>Vajra1yudha (Vajra weapon) against Bhr2gu's wife,
<>Puloma1. Under the stroke of Vajra she fell down, a
<>headless corpse. The enraged Mahars2i Bhr2gu cursed
<>Maha1vis2n2u to be born as a mortal in this world and to
<>suffer the pangs of separation from his wife. When the
<>curse was pronounced against Maha1vis2n2u, he directed
<>his weapon Cakra against the Mahars2i. Bhr2gu fied in
<>panic and at last begged pardon and prayed for shelter
<>to Maha1vis2n2u himself in the ocean of milk. Vis2n2u
<>withdrew his Cakra. Bhr2gu himself restored Puloma1
<>to life. To fulfil the condition of Bhr2gu's curse, Vis2n2u
<>agreed to incarnate in the world as S4ri1 Ra1ma, the son
<>of Das4aratha and to experience the pain of separation
<>from his wife. (Uttara Ra1ma1yan2a).
<NI>5) {%Bhr2gu kicked Vis2n2u.%} Long ago all the Mahars2is
<>joined together to perform a ya1ga on the bank of the
<>river Sarasvati1. A dispute arose among them as to who
<>was the most mighty among the Trimu1rtis. Some of
<>them voted for Brahma1, others declared that Vis2n2u
<>was more mighty than the other two, while a third
<>group stood for S4iva's superiority. They unanimously
<>elected Bhr2gu to ascertain and find out the truth of
<>the matter. [Page140-b+ 43]
<NI>Bhr2gu set out to Devaloka. First he went to Brahma1's
<>assembly. There, in the presence of Brahma1 who was
<>seated in the midst of many Munis, Bhr2gu took his seat
<>on a stool. Brahma1 was provoked by this act of disres-
<>pect. Bhr2gu left the place without a word and went to
<>S4iva's place. S4iva rose from his seat and approached
<>him to embrace and welcome him. Bhr2gu, shrank back
<>saying, “Do not touch me?” S4iva became angry and
<>was about to hit him with his trident when Pa1rvati1
<>stopped him.
<NI>Bhr2gu then turned his steps to Vaikun2t2ha, the abode of
<>Maha1vis2n2u. There he saw Maha1vis2n2u in a deep
<>slumber. Seeing Maha1vis2n2u whose task is the pre-
<>servation of the world, sleeping like an irresponsible
<>person, Bhr2gu gave him a kick on his breast. Vis2n2u
<>who sprang up suddenly, saw Bhr2gu standing before
<>him. He begged pardon of the sage. He declared that
<>he would carry Bhr2gu's footprint permanently on his
<>chest as a sign of his repentance for having shown dis-
<>respect to the Mahars2i. This foot-print still remains
<>on Vis2n2u's chest and is known by the name “S4ri1vatsa”.
<>In this way, the Munis came to the conclusion that
<>Maha1vis2n2u is the noblest of the Trimu1rtis. (Bha1gavata,
<>Das4ama Skandha).
<NI>6) {%The origin of Bhr2gu Ti1rtha.%} There is a sacred spot
<>called, “Bhr2gu Ti1rtha” on the western side of Das4a1s4va-
<>medha. It is here that Bhr2gu once offered tapas to S4iva.
<>Owing to the austerity of his tapas, his hair became
<>matted and discoloured. His body was completely
<>covered with earth heaped up by termites. When S4iva
<>was still not propitiated, Pa1rvati1 interceded with him
<>on behalf of Bhr2gu, S4iva agreed to bless Bhr2gu.
<NI>S4iva sent his bull to the place where Bhr2gu was sitting.
<>The bull in the course of its gambols broke up and des-
<>troyed the earthen covering on his body which was
<>made by the termites. Bhr2gu became angry and chased
<>the bull. But he was stunned by the sight of the bull
<>rising up to heaven through the air. A divine light
<>spread there. S4iva appeared before him and asked him
<>what boon he wanted. Bhr2gu prayed that the place
<>where he was doing tapas should become a holy spot.
<>S4iva granted his prayer and from that day, the place
<>became famous under the name “Bhr2gu Ti1rtha”. [Page141-a+ 62]
<>Brahma1 and other Devas and the Kinnaras still worship
<>this Bhr2gu Ti1rtha. All sin is removed by a mere sight
<>of this sacred Ti1rtha. Those who bathe in the holy
<>water of this place attain Heaven and they will not be
<>born again. Even by hearing about the greatness and
<>glory of this Bhr2gu Ti1rtha, one will be cleared of all
<>sins and find an easy way to S4ivaloka. (Padma Pura1n2a,
<>Chapter 20).

<HI>BHR2N3GI1. A Mahars2i who was a devotee of S4iva. Once

<HI>BHU1MI I. The earth.
<NI>1) {%General.%} The Pura1n2as maintain that Bhu1mi has a
<>Devi1 (goddess). The births of Bhu1mi and its basic
<>goddess are in two different ways.
<NI>The Maha1bha1rata, (Da1ks2in2a1tya Pa1t2ha) says that the
<>goddess Bhu1mi was the daughter of Brahma1 and that
<>she was married by Maha1vis2n2u. The earth on which
<>we live is the Mr2tpin2d2a of which the basic deity is this
<>Bhu1midevi1. Of the many versions given in the Pura1n2as
<>regarding the origin of earth, three are given below:--
<NI>1) Long ago, towards the end of the age of floods, the
<>earth was in a liquid state. At that time, S4iva cut open
<>his thigh and let fall a drop of blood in the water.
<>It assumed the form of an “an2d2a” (egg). S4iva took that
<>an2d2a and split it. A man came out of it. From him was
<>made Nature (Prakr2ti) for the creation of the Universe.
<>One half of the broken an2d2a became sky and the other
<>half became the earth. (Katha1saritsa1gara, Katha1pi1t2ha-
<>lam3baka, 2nd Taran3ga).
<NI>(2) Maha1vis2n2u lay on the surface of water which spread
<>everywhere in the beginning. A lotus sprang up from [Page142-b+ 62]
<>the navel of Vis2n2u and from its top Brahma1 was born.
<>Liquid matter began to flow out of Vis2n2u's ears on both
<>sides. From it were born two Ra1ks2asas named Madhu
<>and Kait2abha. They persecuted Brahma1. Maha1vis2n2u
<>woke up and killed Madhu and Kait2abha. The thick
<>fat of these Ra1ks2asas hardened into the earth. (Devi1
<>Bha1gavata, Navama Skandha).
<NI>3) In the beginning Maha1vis2n2u (Maha1vira1t2 Purus2a)
<>spread everywhere. In every pore of that Maha1vira1t2
<>who was lying on the surface of the water, there was a
<>Brahma1n2d2a. In course of time that Vira1t2 obtained mind.
<>That mind stood connected with each of the pores
<>equally. Later from it were formed the “Pan5camaha1-
<>bhu1tas”. From their combination was formed the Bhu1ta
<>called “Maha1 Pr2thvi1”. It was cut into many pieces
<>and each of the pieces was deposited in each pore.
<>It was these Pr2thvi1 pieces which became “Bhu1mis”
<>at the time of creation. At the time of the floods, these
<>Bhu1mis sank again into those pores as before. In each
<>of these Brahma1n2d2as, there are the earth, mountains,
<>forests, oceans, the seven islands, Himava1n, Meru,
<>Sun, Moon, Stars and other planets. Also, each of
<>them has its own Brahma1, Vis2n2u, S4iva and other Devas.
<>Since all the different Bhu1mis in all the Brahma1n2d2as
<>had been formed artificially, they all perish in the floods.
<>(Devi1 Bha1gavata, Navama Skandha).
<NI>3) Bhu1mi Devi1 (Goddess Earth) is the wife of Maha1
<>Vis2n2u. In Vara1ha Kalpa (Age of the Pig) the Asura
<>Hiran2ya1ks2a carried the Earth and Submerged it under
<>water. At once Maha1 vis2n2u appeared in the form of a
<>Pig and lifted up the Earth on its horns. When the Earth
<>floated on the surface of water like a lotus leaf, Bhu1mi
<>Devi1 who was pleased, stood up in her charming figure.
<>Maha1vis2n2u fell in love with her and with the brilliance
<>of a crore of suns, had sexual union with her for the
<>period of one Devavars2a. It is from that time that
<>Bhu1mi Devi1 became Maha1vis2n2u's wife. As a result
<>of their union, a son named Man3gala was born to
<>them.
<NI>Ghat2es4a is the son of Man3gala. Man3gala has another
<>name, Covva. After the birth of Man3gala, at the behest
<>of Lord Vis2n2u, all people began to offer worship to
<>Bhu1midevi1. Maha1vis2n2u himself first worshipped her
<>by reciting the mantra--“Om Hri1m3-S4ri1m3-Kri1m3-Vasu-
<>dha1yai Sva1ha1”. After that this mantra became popular

<NI>Naraka1sura was Bhu1midevi1's son by Hiran2ya1ks2a, the

<NI>4) {%Bhu1mi and Prahla1da.%} Since Bhu1midevi1 had been the

<HI>BHUS4UN2D2A. A dispassionate and large-hearted crow.
<>The residence of this crow was a Kalpavr2ks2a standing
<>on a beautiful peak surrounded by luxuriant vegetation
<>in the north-eastern corner of Maha1meru. There were
<>numerous bird-nests on the southern branch of that
<>Kalpavr2ks2a. In one of them lived this centuries-old
<>bird.
<NI>Once when the sage Vasis2t2ha went to Devaloka, he
<>happened to hear about this crow. He went to see
<>Bhus4un2d2a in its nest. The crow recognised Vasis2t2ha
<>at once. They exchanged greetings. The sage opened
<>the conversation as follows:--“Oh, King of birds!
<>when were you born? How did you become a great
<>soul? How old are you? Have you recollections of the
<>past? Who was the prophet who suggested this residence
<>for you?”
<NI>The bird calmly replied as follows:--“If you are interes-
<>ted in hearing my past history I shall tell you. Lord
<>S4an3kara the Almighty lives in this world. He has numer-
<>ous attendant spirits. Besides these spirits who have
<>hoofs on their head, hands in the hoofs, teeth in
<>the hands and stomach in the face, and who have faces
<>resembling those of monkeys, camels, and elephants,
<>he has also hordes of Ma1tr2s in his retinue. The Ma1tr2s,
<>attended by spirits continue their dance in the presence
<>of the Lord. Mountain peaks, the sky, the different
<>worlds, deep pits, cremation grounds, etc. are their
<>haunts. Chief among these Ma1tr2s are eight sisters
<>named, Jaya1, Vijaya1, Jayanti1, Apara1hita1, Siddha1,
<>Rakta1, Alambus2a1 and Ulpala1. They have other follow-
<>ers also. Alambus2a1's vehicle is the crow named Can2d2a. [Page144-b+ 65]
<>All these Ma1tr2s assembled together on one occasion to
<>celebrate a festival in the sky. There was a display of
<>many kinds of entertainments at that time. Disputations
<>in spiritual matters, music, dancing, drinking and other
<>forms of hilarious activities were freely indulged in.
<>In another part of the sky, their vehicles were also
<>enjoying themselves with similar celebrations of drinking,
<>dancing, and merry-making. The swans who were the
<>vehicles of Bra1hmi1devi1 were dancing in one place,
<>intoxicated by drink. Can2d2a, the crow, who was Alam-
<>bus2a1's vehicle, also joined their company. Completely
<>absorbed in their delirious raptures, the intoxicated
<>swans indulged so freely in their amorous pleasures with
<>Can2d2a that they became pregnant. At last when the
<>merry-makings ended and all of them dispersed, the swans
<>became aware of their plight and informed Bra1hmi1
<>about it. The gracious goddess (Bra1hmi1) told them
<>that in their present state they were unable to discharge
<>their duties in drawing her chariot and so they were allow-
<>ed to go and enjoy themselves wherever they liked. After
<>this she entered into a trance. The swans in the fullness
<>of time, gave birth to twentyone sons. We, the twenty-
<>one brothers, are those children. We and our mothers
<>went to Bra1hmi1devi1 and offered worship to her for a
<>long time. As a result, the Devi1 woke up from her trance
<>and pleased with us, gave us her blessing. After that,
<>we went to our father (Can2d2a) and off red our devoted
<>services to him and prostrated before him and Alam-
<>bus2a1devi1. They blessed us. We asked our father to
<>suggest a most suitable place for a secluded life. This
<>Kalpa Vr2ks2a is the secluded place recommended by
<>him. We paid obeisance to our father and Alambu-
<>s2a1devi1 and came to settle down here. Many ages have
<>passed since then. Now your visit and holy presence
<>here, have liberated me from all worldly bonds and
<>ennobled my life. My twenty brothers lived for many
<>Kalpas and yugas at the end of which, convinced of the
<>meaninglessness of worldly life, renounced their bodies
<>and attained S4ivaloka.
<NI>On hearing this, Vasis2t2ha asked Bhus4un2d2a to tell him
<>more about his past life. Bhus4un2d2a resumed his story:--
<>“Long long ago, the whole earth was full of big rocks,
<>without trees, forests or mountains. After a great flood
<>the surface of the earth was covered with ashes. In
<>one caturyuga (a period equal to the length of the four
<>yugas, Kr2ta, treta1, dva1para and Kali) the earth was
<>filled with forest trees and in another Caturyuga, moun-
<>tain ranges appeared. I have seen an age in which
<>Bra1hman2as were drunkards, S4u1dras were virtuous and
<>women of noble families committed adultery. You
<>have now been born in the eightieth “Janma” as the
<>son of Brahma1. You were born once from the sky, at
<>another time from water, then from the mountain and
<>again from fire. I can remember this earth sinking into
<>the ocean five times and Lord Vis2n2u taking the form of
<>a tortoise, lifting it up, above the water. I have seen the
<>ocean of milk being churned twelve times. I know that
<>Hiran2ya1ks2a had taken the earth three times to Pa1ta1la
<>(underworld). The Lord has incarnated six times as
<>Bha1rgava Ra1ma. Incarnation of Buddha has taken
<>place in six Kaliyugas. Tripuradahana (burning of
<>the Tripura1suras) has taken place thirty times. Daks2a
<>ya1ga was broken up twice. Lord S4iva has slain ten
<>Indras. He fought seven times with S4ri1 Kr2s2n2a for the
<>sake of Ba1n2a. I also remember another epic entitled [Page145-a+ 65]
<>“Ra1ma1yan2a”, containing one lakh of verses and dealing
<>with metaphysical problems. I have seen the customs
<>of Kr2tayuga being followed in Kaliyuga and the customs
<>of Kaliyuga being followed in Kr2tayuga.”
<NI>Having heard the whole story, Vasis2t2ha gave his blessing
<>to Bhus4un2d2a and left the place. (Jn5a1na Va1sis2t2ha,
<>Bhu un2d2opa1khya1na).

<HI>BHU1TAS. (A set of beings created by Rudra).
<NI>1) {%General.%} A Ma1nava class or sect in ancient India.
<>In the Pura1n2as, this Ma1nava sect is classified into four
<>subdivisions. (1) Dharmapraja (2) I1s4varapraja (3)
<>Ka1s4yapi1yapraja (4) Pulahapraja.
<NI>2) {%Birth.%} In the Brahma1n2d2a Pura1n2a there is the follow-
<>ing story about the birth and shape of Bhu1tas:--
<NI>Bhu1tas are one of the subdivisions of Pulaha's creations.
<>Long ago, Brahma1 asked the Rudra, Ni1lalohita, to
<>perform the function of creation. Accordingly he begot
<>thousands of Bhu1tas in the womb of his wife Sati1. All
<>the issues were the exact replica of his own figure.
<>Lean limbs, long ears, thick hanging lips, red eyes, bushy
<>eyebrows, long, pointed and protruding teeth, long nails,
<>matted dirty hair etc. were the grotesque features of
<>these Bhu1tas. These music-haters used serpents as their
<>Yajn5opavi1tas (sacred threads). These spirits who loitered
<>in S4iva's assembly were, as a rule, naked and carried
<>skulls on their heads. But at times they wore fantastic
<>dress with elephant skin. Their chief weapons were,
<>trident, bow, sword, etc.
<NI>3) {%Bhu1ta Chief.%} In the Pura1n2as, Rudra is acknowledged
<>as the Bhu1ta chief. That is why Rudra is known by such
<>names as “Bhu1tana1yaka”, “Gan2ana1yaka”, “Rudra1nu-
<>cara”, “Bhavaparis2ada” etc. But since the common
<>name Rudra is used for the ruler (king) of all the
<>Bhu1tas, Va1mana Pura1n2a declares that Rudra is not an
<>individual. Both Va1manapura1n2a and Matsyapura1n2a
<>represent Vi1rabhadra and Nandikes4vara as two Rudras
<>who are the masters of Bhu1tas. (Matsyapura1n2a 181,
<>2; Va1manapura1n2a 4, 17).
<NI>In Va1mana Pura1n2a, the number of Bhu1tas is given as
<>11 crores. S4kanda, Sa1kha, Bhairava are the chief among
<>them. Under them are innumerable Bhu1tas. Ashes [Page145-b+ 65]
<>and Khatva1m3ga etc. are their weapons. The emblem
<>on the banner is a cow or a bird. That is how the
<>Gan2ana1yakas have got the titles like “Mayu1radhvaja”,
<>“Mayu1rava1hana”. (Va1mana Pura1n2a 67, 1-23).
<NI>4) {%War with Asuras.%} In the war between S4iva and
<>Andhaka1sura, the Bhu1tas fought on the side of S4iva.
<>It was Vina1yaka, the master of the Bhu1ta hordes who
<>first came into conflict with the Asura. In that battle
<>Andhaka defeated Vina1yaka. After that, Nandi, an-
<>other leader of the Bhu1tas, attacked Andhaka jointly
<>with Vina1yaka and defeated him. At last, Andhaka
<>approached S4iva himself for protection, and S4iva received
<>him and appointed him as commander of one of his
<>hordes of Bhu1tas. It is this Andhaka1sura who later
<>became famous under the name of Bhr2n3gi.
<NI>In this way, the Bhu1tas had fought many battles with
<>the Asuras, joining the party of the Devas. But at the
<>time of Daks2a's yajn5a, they joined the party of the Asuras
<>and opposed the Devas.
<NI>Although the Bhu1tas won all the battles they fought both
<>on the side of the Devas and on the side of the Asuras,
<>in the end they had to leave north India and to come and
<>settle down in south India. By the time of Vaivasvata
<>manvantara they had already become South Indians.

<HI>BILVA. (VILVA). A devotee of Vis2n2u. There is a

<NI>In the beginning Brahma1 created many things among

<HI>BODHISATTVA. A good-natured husband generally
<>quoted in Sanskrit works. The following is the story
<>given about him in Katha1saritsa1gara, Taran3ga 9.
<NI>Once there lived a wealthy Vais4ya, who had a son named
<>Bodhisattva. When the childhood of the boy was at an
<>end his mother died. The Vais4ya married again and got
<>his son also married. Because of the ear-buzzing of his
<>wife, the Vais4ya drove his son out of the house. Bodhi-
<>sattva left the house of his father, with his wife. By
<>and by they reached a desert. Not a drop of water was to
<>be had. There was not even the shoot of a grass. It was a
<>sandy place with nothing else in sight. He walked for
<>seven days carrying his wife on his shoulders. His wife
<>grew weary and worn with hunger and thirst. Seeing
<>that she was about to die he gave her his flesh and blood.
<>The wicked woman took them and saved herself from
<>death. On the eighth day they reached the jungles of a
<>hilly place full of fruit-trees and with a river with grassy
<>banks, flowing down to the valley. With fruits and cool
<>water he appeased the hunger and thirst of his wife.
<>Then he got down to the river to take a bath. He saw
<>a man with his limbs cut off, coming afloat. Now and
<>then he was producing pitiable sounds. The kind son of
<>the Vais4ya, without minding his weakness due to fast for
<>the last seven days, swam to the man and brought him to
<>the bank of the river. He did all services possible for him.
<>Then he asked him who had cut off his limbs. He rep-
<>lied that his enemies had done so, with the intention that
<>he might die suffering severe pain for a long time. The
<>Vais4ya's son stood still for a little while. Then he took
<>his bath. With his wife he lived in the forest doing
<>penance. The wounds of the man he saved had been
<>healed. The Vais4ya's son, one day, went out to the
<>forest to gather fruits and roots for their food. At that
<>time his wife grew lustful and had coition with the man
<>without limbs. Gradually she began to dote on him. She
<>decided to kill her husband who was an impediment on
<>her way. She pretended to be ill. The Vais4ya's son began
<>to treat her. One day she took her husband to the edge of
<>a very deep well and said: “See, there is a divine herb at
<>the bottom of this well. I will be cured if I could eat it.
<>This is what a goddess told me in a dream yesternight”.
<>Hearing this her husband made a rope, and tied it to a
<>tree. Then he began to go down the well by the rope.
<>She cut the rope and the man fell into the well. There
<>was a passage from the well to the river. The current
<>took him through that passage to the river. He got out of
<>the river, and sat under a tree thinking of the wickedness
<>of women. There was a city close by. At that time the
<>King of the city was dead and there was no heir left. The
<>subjects of the city brought an elephant and said, “whom
<>ever this elephant takes and places on his back shall be
<>our king”. They sent the elephant out. The elephant [Page147-a+ 64]
<>was pleased at the virtuous character of the son of the
<>Vais4ya. So taking him, as if he was God, placed him on
<>its back and walked to the city. The people gathered
<>round him and anointed him as their King. The son of
<>the Vais4ya became King. He never even thought of
<>women who are generally fickle and wicked.
<NI>The wicked wife of the Vais4ya's son took the limbless
<>man on her shoulder and wandered about saying, “The
<>enemies of my husband have put him in this plight.
<>Because of my conjugal fidelity I carry him thus and
<>earn our daily bread. Please give us alms”. In this
<>manner she spent her days in begging. Thus wandering
<>from place to place she reached the city where the
<>Vaisya's son was the King. The people, seeing her
<>loyalty to her husband, honoured her and spoke highly
<>of her. Hearing that a very loyal wife had reached his
<>city the King sent for her. The King recognized her
<>instantly. But she did not know him. The King reminded
<>her of her deeds of the past one by one and began to
<>tease and scold her. Finally when she understood that
<>the King was her husband she was dumb-founded. The
<>amazed ministers looked at each other. The King reveal-
<>ed everything to them. The ministers disfigured her and
<>drove her away.
<HI>BODHYA. A famous teacher-priest. Once there was a

<NI>Before I advise others, I do it myself first. I am the tea-
<>cher of none. I take the world as my teacher. I learned

<>from Pin3gala the harlot, self-sacrifice from animals,

<NI>This hermit came to the King Yaya1ti and taught him

<HI>BRAHMA1:
<NI>One of the trimu1rtis of the Hindu Pantheon. The tri-
<>mu1rtis are Brahma1, Vis2n2u and S4iva.
<NI>1) {%General information.%} God who is the creator of the
<>Universe. It is mentioned in the Pura1n2as that Brahma1
<>creates, Vis2n2u preserves and Paramas4iva destroys the
<>universe.
<NI>2) {%The birth of Brahma1.%} The birth of Brahma1 is from
<>the nave of Vis2n2u. It is mentioned in Devi1 Pura1n2a,
<>Skandha 1, about the birth of Brahma1 as follows:--
<>In the beginning Maha1vis2n2u lay on a banian leaf in the
<>shape of a baby and began to think, “Who am I? Who
<>created me? What for? What is my work? Where to
<>work?” and so on. At that time an ethereal voice said:--
<>“Sarvam3 khalvidameva1ham3 na1nyadasti sana1ta-
<>nam”.
<F>*) Idam3 sarvam3 khalu aham eva, Sana1tanam anyad na1sti. All these are myself. Except me there is nothing eternal.</F> Maha1vis2n2u was amazed at this ethereal
<>voice. He did not know whose oracle it was. Still He
<>lay meditating upon the words. Then Maha1devi1,
<>with four hands and weapons such as S4an3kha (conch),
<>Cakra (wheel), Gada1 (club), Padma (lotus) and
<>maids who are prosperities and having worn glorious
<>clothes and ornaments, and accompanied by the S4aktis [Page147-b+ 63]
<>(powers) named Rati, Bhu1ti, Buddhi, Mati, Ki1rti,
<>Dhr2ti, Smr2ti, S4raddha1, Medha1, Svadha1, Sva1ha1, Ks2udha1,
<>Nidra1, Daya1, Gati1, Tus2t2i, Pus2t2i, Ks2ama1, Lajja1, Jr2m3bha1
<>and Tandra1, appeared before Maha1vis2n2u, who was
<>struck with wonder. Maha1devi1 said, “Oh, Vis2n2u, what
<>is there to wonder at? Every time the universe is sub-
<>jected to creation, preservation and destruction, you
<>are born thus due to the great power of the supreme
<>spirit. It seems that you have forgotten those matters.
<>Know that the supreme power is beyond qualities. We
<>are all with qualities. Your main quality is Sattva.
<>From your nave Brahma1 will be born. His attribute is
<>Rajogun2a (activity, passion or motion). From the middle
<>of the eyebrows of Brahma1, will be born Rudra, whose
<>attribute will be Ta1masagun2a (darkness). Brahma1,
<>with the power of penance, will acquire the ability of
<>creation and by his attribute of Rajogun2a will create
<>the world in the colour of blood. You will be the preserver
<>of that world. The same world will be destroyed by
<>Rudra at the end of the Kalpa (world age)”.
<NI>Accordingly from the nave of Vis2n2u a lotus grew up and
<>in that lotus flower Brahma1 took his form. The same
<>Brahmadeva did penance before Maha1vis2n2u and Jaga-
<>damba1, who were pleased at his penance and gave him
<>all the boons he wanted. After that Brahma1 began the
<>work of creation. He created with his mind the Saptars2is,
<>(seven sages) and then the Praja1patis (the lords of
<>emanation). From them all the movables and the
<>immovables in the universe came into existence. (Devi1
<>Bha1gavata, Skandha 7).
<NI>In manusmr2ti, Chapter 1, the following stanza about the
<>creation of Brahma1 occurs.
<Poem>“Tadan2d2amabhavad haimam
<>Sahasra1m3s4usamaprabham3 /
<>Tasmin jajn5e svayam3 Brahma1
<>Sarvalokapita1mahah2” //</Poem>
<NI>That egg was as radiant as the Sun, with the colour of
<>gold. Brahma1 the great grandfather of everything in the
<>world took birth by himself in it.
<NI>From the supreme power, an egg fell on the water which
<>was the first creation. That egg became a germ of golden
<>colour. Creating a life, which had done penance in its
<>former births in such a way as to enable it to become
<>Brahma1, in the golden germ of the egg, the supreme power
<>entered the life that is to become Brahma1 as its inner
<>guide. That Brahma1 is known as the Pita1maha (Grand-
<>father of the manes) or Paternal grandfather of all the
<>worlds.”
<NI>Va1manapura1n2a Chapter 43 states as follows about the
<>creation of Brahma1:--
<NI>Ages before the beginning, when all the worlds with
<>everything they contained were submerged in the single
<>ocean of the great flood, the germ of living things formed
<>itself into a big egg. Brahma1 who had been inside the
<>egg went to a long sleep. The sleep continued for a
<>thousand yugas (ages) when Brahma1 woke up; as
<>Sattva gun2a (purity) was the foremost attribute of him,
<>he saw that the world was void. When the thought of
<>creation occurred in his mind Rajogun2a (activity or
<>passion) became his foremost attribute. Rajas is the
<>attribute that creates and Sattva, that which preserves.
<>At the time of destruction Tamogun2a (darkness) be-
<>comes the foremost attribute. That Bhagava1n (Supreme [Page148-a+ 64]
<>Spirit) the Purus2a (the Male creative Energy) pervades
<>over everything, in all the living worlds. That Eternal
<>Being is Brahma1, Vis2n2u, S4iva.
<NI>Knowing that the world was lying in pure water, the
<>Bhagava1n (Supreme Being) cut the egg open. From it the

<NI>5) {%The loss of a head.%} Long ago S4iva plucked off a head
<>of Brahma1. This story occurs in various pura1n2as with
<>slight changes. Two of them are given below:--
<NI>(1) In olden days, in the period of Satyayuga, Maha1-
<>vis2n2u did penance in S4vetadvi1pa (the island S4veta)
<>to obtain Eternal Bliss, being deeply engaged in the study

<>Both were doing severe penance. So they began to

<>other also asked the same question. The talk ended in a

<>claimed himself to be the supreme power of the world.
<>Neither of them was prepared to recognize the claims
<>of the other. In the midst of this contest, a phallus,
<>extra-ordinarily bulky and fair appeared before them and
<>an ethereal voice said from the sky: “You need not
<>quarrel as to who is superior. He who reaches the extre-
<>mity of this phallus is the superior person. So both of
<>you proceed, one upwards and the other downwards
<>and find out the end.” Hearing this Vis2n2u went down-
<>wards to find out the bottom and Brahma1, upwards to
<>the top. Vis2n2u travelled for a long time and finding no
<>end thought the attempt futile and returned to the start-
<>ing point with disappointment and sat down.
<NI>Brahma1 travelled upwards for a long time and found no
<>end. On the way he saw the petal of a pan2d2a1nus flower,
<>coming down from the sky. Brahma1 took it and joyfully
<>returned and said haughtily to Vis2n2u: “See, I have

<>brought this to convince you. You have been defeated.
<>So can you not admit that I am the superior?”
<>Maha1vis2n2u did not believe the words of Brahma1. So he
<>called the Pan2d2a1nus flower to him and questioned it.
<>The Pan2d2a1nus flower took false oath and witnessed in

<>hand to be on his side. Maha1vis2n2u did not believe

<>S4iva at these words appeared before them and revealed

<>of Brahma1. That is the skull S4iva uses for receiving
<>alms. (Devi1 Bha1gavata, S4kandha 5.)
<NI>(2) In days of old all the worlds with everything in them
<>were under water in a single ocean. The Sun, the
<>Moon, the Stars, air, fire, everything was destroyed. A
<>day of utter darkness appeared. Grass, bush all were

<NI>8) {%Brahma1 became river.%} Long ago in the period of

<NI>Thus Brahma1, Vis2n2u and Mahes4vara became rivers

<NI>9) {%Brahma1 is not worshipped.%} Long ago Brahma1 and

<NI>(10) In Maha1bha1rata, Anus4a1sana Parva there is a

<NI>Lord Rudra took the form of Varun2a and performed a

<>is the ether and the husband of the Earth, is the lord
<>of all accomplishments, is noble and the lord of radiance.
<>This Lord is lauded by the names Brahma1, S4iva, Rudra,
<>Varun2a, Agni, and Prabha1vati1. S4iva is the King of all
<>the worlds. Penances, sacrifices, vows emblazed by fast,
